song</td><td>Eliminated</td></tr></tbody></table><p>Soon after being eliminated from <i>The X Factor</i>, Devlin performed some gigs at various venues throughout the UK. One of these was the renowned G-A-Y venue on Saturday, 3 December 2011.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-14” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[14]</a>[<i><a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FWikipedia%3AVerifiability” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>not in citation given</a></i>] Finishing fifth, she was one of nine acts to perform on the <i>X Factor</i> Live Tour 2012, which took place in cities throughout the UK and Ireland.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-15” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[15]</a> She performed fan favourite cover songs, ‘Fix You’ and ‘Sweet Child o’ Mine’.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-16” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[16]</a></p><h3>2012–13: <i>Hide &amp; Seek</i>[<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fw%2Findex.php%3Ftitle%3DJanet_Devlin%26action%3Dedit%26section%3D5%26editintro%3DTemplate%3ABLP_editintro” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>edit</a>]</h3><p>It was reported that Devlin had received at least three offers of a recording contract.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-17” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[17]</a> Within hours of leaving the show Devlin had been offered a recording contract by RKA Records, a record company partly owned by <i><a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FDragons%2527_Den” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Dragons’ Den</a></i> star and entrepreneur <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FDuncan_Bannatyne” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Duncan Bannatyne</a>.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-18” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[18]</a></p><p>Following the <i>X Factor</i> Live Tour, Devlin began work on her debut album at Steelworks Recording Studios, Sheffield. She was first in the recording studio on 28 May 2012, where she wrote and recorded three songs (‘Crown of Thorns’,<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-19” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[19]</a> ‘Thinking Back Yesterday’<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-20” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[20]</a> and ‘Who Am I Today?’<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-21” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[21]</a>) with <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FGrammy_Award” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Grammy Award</a> and <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fw%2Findex.php%3Ftitle%3DIvor_Novella_Award%26action%3Dedit%26redlink%3D1” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Ivor Novella Award</a>-winning producer <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FEliot_Kennedy” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Eliot Kennedy</a><a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-Eliot_Kennedy-22” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[22]</a> and his team. The song &quot;Crown of Thorns&quot;, which was one of the first she wrote, with Jim Jayawardena and <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FPhilippa_Hanna” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Philippa Hanna</a> (of Kennedy’s Steelworks team), quickly became an addition to her live sets at gigs.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-23” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[23]</a></p><p>Devlin has written all of her songs, usually with one co-writer, for inclusion on her debut album. She has written with songwriters Joe Janiak, <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FHelen_Boulding” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Helen Boulding</a><a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-24” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[24]</a> and <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FEthan_Ash” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Ethan Ash</a>.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-25” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[25]</a> She has also written potential tracks for her debut release with songwriters including the Faulkner brothers, Toby and <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FNewton_Faulkner” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Newton Faulkner</a>,<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-ulsterherald-26” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[26]</a> <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJoshua_Radin” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Joshua Radin</a><a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-27” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[27]</a> and <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJack_Savoretti” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Jack Savoretti</a>.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-28” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[28]</a> In 2013, Devlin stated in interviews that she had written around 25 songs and would continue to write more songs to have the best possible finished album.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-29” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[29]</a> On 26 October 2012, she debuted two new, live edition, songs on her YouTube channel. They were &quot;Wonderful&quot; which was co-written with <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FNewton_Faulkner” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Newton Faulkner</a> and the aforementioned &quot;Crown of Thorns&quot;.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-30” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[30]</a></p><p>Devlin’s debut album was launched on <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FPledge_Music” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Pledge Music</a>, including a chance to record backing vocals with her<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-31” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[31]</a> (although that never happened). In December 2012, it was stated that the album would be released in 2013, having reached 45% of the pledge target within the first two weeks.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-Dean-32” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[32]</a> Having reached 100% on New Year’s Eve 2012, Devlin began the recording of her album in early 2013. On 26 June 2013, she finished recording the limited release version of her debut album. <i>Hide &amp; Seek</i> was released to pledgers on 1 July 2013.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-33” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[33]</a> Janet released an exclusive bonus acoustic EP, <i>Nothing Lost</i>, to pledgers on 14 August 2013.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-34” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[34]</a></p><p>On 25 June 2013, Devlin worked with Newton Faulkner again, providing vocals for his new album project, #studiozoo. She provided backing vocals for 2 tracks as well as lending her voice for more of a featured backing vocal on a track called &quot;Plastic Hearts&quot;.[<i><a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FWikipedia%3ACitation_needed” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>citation needed</a></i>] A live version of her song &quot;Things We Lost in the Fire&quot; was premiered on her YouTube channel on 6 December 2013.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-35” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[35]</a></p><h3>2014–present: <i>Running with Scissors</i>[<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fw%2Findex.php%3Ftitle%3DJanet_Devlin%26action%3Dedit%26section%3D6%26editintro%3DTemplate%3ABLP_editintro” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>edit</a>]</h3><p>In early January 2014, Devlin debuted a new live version of her song &quot;Delicate&quot;, (written with Jack Savoretti and a new addition to the general release album) performing with Tom Dibb (guitar and vocals), in a <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FBalconyTV” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>BalconyTV</a> session.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-36” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[36]</a> She won the Balcony TV Global Music Rumble two weeks in a row on the 2 and 9 March and again on the 23 March.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-37” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[37]</a><a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-38” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[38]</a><a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-39” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[39]</a></p><p>Devlin announced in March 2014 that the general release of her debut album, with the new title <i>Running with Scissors</i> would be on 9 June. The album would feature new single &quot;House of Cards&quot; (to be released on 26 May)<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-40” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[40]</a> with 3 other new original songs (&quot;Whisky Lullabies&quot; co written with UK songwriter Tim Jennings, &quot;Lifeboat&quot; and &quot;When You Were Mine&quot;), a cover of <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FThe_Cure” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>The Cure</a>’s &quot;<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FFriday_I%2527m_in_Love” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Friday I’m in Love</a>&quot; and reworked versions of &quot;Delicate&quot; (from the EP <i>Nothing Lost</i>), &quot;Wonderful&quot;, &quot;Creatures of the Night&quot;, &quot;Things We Lost in the Fire&quot; and &quot;Hide &amp; Seek&quot; from the limited release album <i>Hide &amp; Seek</i>. The reworked version of the song &quot;Hide &amp; Seek&quot; features <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FNewton_Faulkner” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Newton Faulkner</a>who, along with his brother, co-wrote it with Devlin.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-41” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[41]</a> On Oct 12, 2015, Devlin announced she would be using Pledge Music again to launch her preorder of her Christmas EP December Daze. She was featured on <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fw%2Findex.php%3Ftitle%3DShy_and_Drs%26action%3Dedit%26redlink%3D1” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Shy and Drs</a> &quot;Beautiful to Me&quot; which was released on November 13 as the official song for Anti Bullying Week 2015.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-42” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[42]</a> She recently has been featured on <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FGareth_Emery” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Gareth Emery</a>’s new album, <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2F100_Reasons_to_Live” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>100 Reasons to Live</a>, released March 31, 2016. The song &quot;Lost&quot; is a remix of her song &quot;Things We Lost in the Fire&quot;.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-43” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[43]</a></p><h2>Artistry[<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fw%2Findex.php%3Ftitle%3DJanet_Devlin%26action%3Dedit%26section%3D7%26editintro%3DTemplate%3ABLP_editintro” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>edit</a>]</h2><h3>Influences[<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fw%2Findex.php%3Ftitle%3DJanet_Devlin%26action%3Dedit%26section%3D8%26editintro%3DTemplate%3ABLP_editintro” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>edit</a>]</h3><p>Devlin is heavily influenced by alternative artists including <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FCity_and_Colour” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>City and Colour</a>, <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJohn_Frusciante” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>John Frusciante</a>, <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FNirvana_(band)” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Nirvana</a> and <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FDevendra_Banhart” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Devendra Banhart</a>.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-44” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[44]</a> She also notes the <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FRed_Hot_Chili_Peppers” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Red Hot Chili Peppers</a> as a favourite band.[<i><a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FWikipedia%3ACitation_needed” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>citation needed</a></i>]</p><h3>Performances[<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fw%2Findex.php%3Ftitle%3DJanet_Devlin%26action%3Dedit%26section%3D9%26editintro%3DTemplate%3ABLP_editintro” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>edit</a>]</h3><p>In 2012, Devlin performed at <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FCroke_Park” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Croke Park</a>, in front of a capacity 82,300 crowd, as part of the half-time show for the All Ireland Gaelic Football final on 23 September. She performed a cover of ‘Fix You’ and one of her self-penned original songs ‘Walk Away’.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-ulsterherald-26” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[26]</a> She performed at the X Factor <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FNSPCC” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>NSPCC</a> <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FChildline” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Childline</a> Ball on 18 October, again singing her original song ‘Walk Away’ and ‘Fix You’ by Coldplay, helping to raise over half a million pounds for the charity.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-45” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[45]</a> On 3 November, she performed at <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FCasement_Park” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Casement Park</a>, as part of the pre-match entertainment, for the <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FMatch_for_Michaela” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Michaela Foundation</a>’s charity Gaelic Football match in memory of Michaela McAreavey.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-46” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[46]</a></p><p>Devlin performed for the Dalai Lama on 18 April 2013 as part of Northern Ireland charity, Children in Crossfire’s ‘Culture of Compassion’ event in Derry.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-47” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[47]</a> On 12 May 2013, she performed a Pledger only concert at Greystones, Sheffield with a backing band consisting of Roo Walker (guitar, vocals), Jim Jayawardena (keyboard), Doug Harper (drums), <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FShe_Makes_War” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Laura Kidd</a> (bass, vocals) and Michael Giverin (mandolin). The second Pledger only concert took place at London’s Troubadour on 13 May 2013.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-48” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[48]</a></p><p>Devlin played 14 dates across the UK and Ireland, with her band, for her ‘Imaginarium Tour’ in September and October 2013.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-49” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[49]</a> Her second tour was in December 2014 and named the ‘My Delirium Tour’. It had dates across the UK including 2 dates in Northern Ireland. The final stop of the tour was in Devlin’s home town of Omagh.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-50” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[50]</a></p><p>Devlin played 4 gigs in the USA supporting <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FHeffron_Drive” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Heffron Drive</a> on their ‘Happy Mistakes Unplugged’ Tour in early July 2015.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-51” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[51]</a> She placed second in the 2015 Baltic Song Contest, representing Ireland, in Karlshamn, Sweden in July 2015.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-52” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[52]</a></p><h2>Recognition[<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fw%2Findex.php%3Ftitle%3DJanet_Devlin%26action%3Dedit%26section%3D10%26editintro%3DTemplate%3ABLP_editintro” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>edit</a>]</h2><p>On 11 May 2012, Devlin was given a Civic Reception by the Town Council in <a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FOmagh” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>Omagh</a>, County Tyrone for her achievements on the X Factor series 8.<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FJanet_Devlin%23cite_note-53” target=”_blank” rel=”nofollow”>[53]</a></p><h2>Discography[<a href=”http://geotrack.email/ext/l?idx=R6D7Iwq9RPOgLg96wyrD&amp;ret=http%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fw%2Findex.php%3Ftitle%3DJanet_Devlin%26action%3Dedit%26section%3D11%26editintro%3DTemplate%3ABLP_editintro”
